list of rules for mapping from distinguished name\" +\n    56→            \" from the client certificate to short name. The rules are evaluated in order and the first rule that matches\" +\n    57→            \" a principal name is used to map it to a short name. Any later rules in the list are ignored. By default,\" +\n    58→            \" distinguished name of the X.500 certificate will be the principal. The rules are evaluated in order and the \" +\n    67→            \"first rule that matches a principal name is used to map it to a short name. Any later rules in the list are \" +\n    68→            \"ignored. If no principal builder is defined, the default behavior depends \" +\n    77→            \"on the security protocol in use. For SSL authentication,  the principal will be derived using the \" +\n    78→            \"rules defined by <code>\" + SSL_PRINCIPAL_MAPPING_RULES_CONFIG + \"</code> applied on the distinguished \" +\n    79→            \"name from the client certificate if one is provided; otherwise, if client authentication is not required, \" +\n    80→            \"the principal name will be ANONYMOUS. javax.security.auth.login.Configuration;\n\n/**\n * JAAS configuration parser that constructs a JAAS configuration object with a single\n * login context from the Kafka configuration option {@link SaslConfigs#SASL_JAAS_CONFIG}.\n * <p/>\n * JAAS configuration file format is described <a href=\"http://docs.oracle.com/javase/8/docs/technotes/guides/security/jgss/tutorials/LoginConfigFile.html\">here</a>.\n * The format of the property value is:\n * <pre>\n * {@code\n *   <loginModuleClass> <controlFlag> (<optionName>=<optionValue>)*;\n * }\n * </pre>\n */\nclass JaasConfig extends Configuration {\n\n    private final String loginContextName;\n    private final List<AppConfigurationEntry> configEntries;\n\n    public JaasConfig(String loginContextName, String jaasConfigParams) {\n        StreamTokenizer tokenizer = new StreamTokenizer(new StringReader(jaasConfigParams));\n        tokenizer.slashSlashComments(true);\n        tokenizer.slashStarComments(true);\n        tokenizer.wordChars('-', '-');\n        tokenizer.wordChars('_', '_');\n        tokenizer.wordChars('$', '$');\n\n        try {\n            configEntries = new ArrayList<>();\n            while (tokenizer.nextToken() != StreamTokenizer.TT_EOF) {\n                configEntries.add(parseAppConfigurationEntry(tokenizer));\n            }\n            if (configEntries.isEmpty())\n                throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Login module not specified in JAAS config\");\n\n            this.loginContextName = loginContextName;\n\n        } catch (IOException e) {\n            throw new KafkaException(\"Unexpected exception while parsing JAAS config\");\n        }\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public AppConfigurationEntry[] getAppConfigurationEntry(String name) {\n        if (this.loginContextName.equals(name))\n            return configEntries.toArray(new AppConfigurationEntry[0]);\n        else\n            return  null;\n    }\n\n    private LoginModuleControlFlag loginModuleControlFlag(String flag) {\n        if (flag == null)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Login module control flag is not available in the JAAS config\");\n\n        LoginModuleControlFlag controlFlag;\n        switch (flag.toUpperCase(Locale.ROOT)) {\n            case \"REQUIRED\":\n                controlFlag = LoginModuleControlFlag.REQUIRED;\n                break;\n            case \"REQUISITE\":\n                controlFlag = LoginModuleControlFlag.REQUISITE;\n                break;\n            case \"SUFFICIENT\":\n                controlFlag = LoginModuleControlFlag.SUFFICIENT;\n                break;\n            case \"OPTIONAL\":\n                controlFlag = LoginModuleControlFlag.OPTIONAL;\n                break;\n            default:\n                throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Invalid login module control flag '\" + flag + \"' in JAAS config\");\n        }\n        return controlFlag;\n    }\n\n    private AppConfigurationEntry parseAppConfigurationEntry(StreamTokenizer tokenizer) throws IOException {\n        String loginModule = tokenizer.sval;\n        if (tokenizer.nextToken() == StreamTokenizer.TT_EOF)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Login module control flag not specified in JAAS config\");\n        LoginModuleControlFlag controlFlag = loginModuleControlFlag(tokenizer.sval);\n        Map<String, String> options = new HashMap<>();\n        while (tokenizer.nextToken() != StreamTokenizer.TT_EOF && tokenizer.ttype != ';') {\n            String key = tokenizer.sval;\n            if (tokenizer.nextToken() != '=' || tokenizer.nextToken() == StreamTokenizer.TT_EOF || tokenizer.sval == null)\n                throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Value not specified for key '\" + key + \"' in JAAS config\");\n            String value = tokenizer.sval;\n            options.put(key, value);\n        }\n        if (tokenizer.ttype != ';')\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"JAAS config entry not terminated by semi-colon\");\n        return new AppConfigurationEntry(loginModule, controlFlag, options);\n    }\n}\n","numLines":125,"startLine":1,"totalLines":125}}}

two levels:\n    58→  * <ul>\n    59→  *   <li>Per-broker configurations are persisted at the controller and can be described\n    60→  *         or altered using AdminClient with the resource name brokerId.</li>\n    61→  *   <li>Cluster-wide default configurations are persisted at the cluster level and can be\n    62→  *         described or altered using AdminClient with an empty resource name.</li>\n    63→  * </ul>\n    64→  * The order of precedence for broker configs is:\n    65→  * <ol>\n    66→  *   <li>STATIC_BROKER_CONFIG: properties that broker is started up with, typically from server.properties file</li>\n    67→  *   <li>DEFAULT_CONFIG: Default configs defined in KafkaConfig</li>\n    68→  * </ol>\n    69→  * Log configs use topic config overrides if defined and fallback to broker defaults using the order of precedence above.\n    70→  * Topic config overrides may use a different config name from the default broker config.\n    71→  * See [[org.apache.kafka.storage.internals.log.LogConfig#TopicConfigSynonyms]] for the mapping.\n    72→  * <p>\n    73→  * AdminClient returns all config synonyms in the order of precedence when configs are described with\n    74→  * <code>includeSynonyms</code>. In addition to configs that may be defined with the same name at different levels,\n    75→  * some configs have additional synonyms.\n    76→  * </p>\n    77→  * <ul>\n    78→  *   <li>Listener configs may be defined using the prefix <tt>listener.name.{listenerName}.{configName}</tt>. These may be\n    79→  *       configured as dynamic or static broker configs. Listener configs have higher precedence than the base configs\n    80→  *       that don't specify the listener name. Listeners without a listener config use the base config. Base configs\n    81→  *       may be defined only as STATIC_BROKER_CONFIG or DEFAULT_CONFIG and cannot be updated dynamically.<li>\n    82→  *   <li>Some configs may be defined using multiple properties. For example, <tt>log.roll.ms</tt> and\n    83→  *       <tt>log.roll.hours</tt> refer to the same config that may be defined in milliseconds or hours. The order of\n    84→  *       precedence of these synonyms is described in the docs of these configs in [[kafka.server.KafkaConfig]].</li>\n    85→  * </ul>\n    86→  *\n    87→  */\n    88→object persisted at the cluster level and can be\n  *         described or altered using AdminClient with an empty resource name.</li>\n  * </ul>\n  * The order of precedence for broker configs is:\n  * <ol>\n  *   <li>STATIC_BROKER_CONFIG: properties that broker is started up with, typically from server.properties file</li>\n  *   <li>DEFAULT_CONFIG: Default configs defined in KafkaConfig</li>\n  * </ol>\n  * Log configs use topic config overrides if defined and fallback to broker defaults using the order of precedence above.\n  * Topic config overrides may use a different config name from the default broker config.\n  * See [[org.apache.kafka.storage.internals.log.LogConfig#TopicConfigSynonyms]] for the mapping.\n  * <p>\n  * AdminClient returns all config synonyms in the order of precedence when configs are described with\n  * <code>includeSynonyms</code>. In addition to configs that may be defined with the same name at different levels,\n  * some configs have additional synonyms.\n  * </p>\n  * <ul>\n  *   <li>Listener configs may be defined using the prefix <tt>listener.name.{listenerName}.{configName}</tt>. These may be\n  *       configured as dynamic or static broker configs. Listener configs have higher precedence than the base configs\n  *       that don't specify the listener name. Listeners without a listener config use the base config. Base configs\n  *       may be defined only as STATIC_BROKER_CONFIG or DEFAULT_CONFIG and cannot be updated dynamically.<li>\n  *   <li>Some configs may be defined using multiple properties. * server side are declared in order, starting with {@link #INITIAL_REQUEST} and\n    99→     * ending in either {@link #COMPLETE} or {@link #FAILED}.\n   100→     * <p>\n   101→     * Re-authentication of a channel on the server side starts with the state\n   102→     * {@link #REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE}. It may then flow to\n   103→     * {@link #REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM} before a transition to {@link #FAILED} if\n   104→     * re-authentication is attempted with a mechanism different than the original\n   105→     * one; otherwise it joins the authentication flow at the {@link #AUTHENTICATE}\n   106→     * state and likewise ends at either {@link #COMPLETE} or {@link #FAILED}.\n   107→     */\n   108→    private enum SaslState {\n   109→        INITIAL_REQUEST,               // May be SaslHandshake or ApiVersions for authentication\n   110→        HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST, // May be SaslHandshake or ApiVersions\n   111→        HANDSHAKE_REQUEST,             // After an ApiVersions request, next request must be SaslHandshake\n   112→        AUTHENTICATE,                  // Authentication tokens (SaslHandshake v1 and above indicate SaslAuthenticate headers)\n   113→        COMPLETE,                      // Authentication completed successfully\n   114→        FAILED,                        // Authentication failed\n   115→        REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE,      // Initial state for re-authentication, processes SASL handshake request\n   116→        REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM,          // When re-authentication requested with wrong mechanism, generate exception\n   117→    }\n   118→\n   119→    private final SecurityProtocol securityProtocol;\n   120→
